 2286 happyTerminalToTok term = case term of {
 2287         TReserved _ "import" -> 2#;
 2288         TReserved _ "submodule" -> 3#;
 2289         TReserved _ "include" -> 4#;
 2290         TReserved _ "include_once" -> 5#;
 2291         TReserved _ "and" -> 6#;
 2292         TReserved _ "as" -> 7#;
 2293         TReserved _ "hiding" -> 8#;
 2294         TReserved _ "let" -> 9#;
 2295         TReserved _ "rec" -> 10#;
 2296         TReserved _ "in" -> 11#;
 2297         TReserved _ "do" -> 12#;
 2298         TReserved _ "if" -> 13#;
 2299         TReserved _ "then" -> 14#;
 2300         TReserved _ "else" -> 15#;
 2301         TReserved _ "typedef" -> 16#;
 2302         TReserved _ "rebindable" -> 17#;
 2303         TReserved _ "ProofScript" -> 18#;
 2304         TReserved _ "TopLevel" -> 19#;
 2305         TReserved _ "CrucibleSetup" -> 20#;
 2306         TReserved _ "CrucibleMethodSpec" -> 21#;
 2307         TReserved _ "LLVMSpec" -> 22#;
 2308         TReserved _ "JVMMethodSpec" -> 23#;
 2309         TReserved _ "JVMSpec" -> 24#;
 2310         TReserved _ "MIRSpec" -> 25#;
 2311         TReserved _ "Bool" -> 26#;
 2312         TReserved _ "Int" -> 27#;
 2313         TReserved _ "String" -> 28#;
 2314         TReserved _ "Term" -> 29#;
 2315         TReserved _ "Type" -> 30#;
 2316         TReserved _ "AIG" -> 31#;
 2317         TReserved _ "CFG" -> 32#;
 2318         TPunct    _ ";" -> 33#;
 2319         TPunct    _ "[" -> 34#;
 2320         TPunct    _ "]" -> 35#;
 2321         TPunct    _ "(" -> 36#;
 2322         TPunct    _ ")" -> 37#;
 2323         TPunct    _ "{" -> 38#;
 2324         TPunct    _ "}" -> 39#;
 2325         TPunct    _ ":" -> 40#;
 2326         TPunct    _ "::" -> 41#;
 2327         TPunct    _ "," -> 42#;
 2328         TPunct    _ "." -> 43#;
 2329         TPunct    _ "\\" -> 44#;
 2330         TPunct    _ "=" -> 45#;
 2331         TPunct    _ "->" -> 46#;
 2332         TPunct    _ "<-" -> 47#;
 2333         TLit      _ _ -> 48#;
 2334         TCode     _ _ -> 49#;
 2335         TCType    _ _ -> 50#;
 2336         TNum      _ _ _ -> 51#;
 2337         TVar      _ _ -> 52#;
 2338         TEOF      _ _ -> 53#;
 2339         _ -> -1#;
 2340         }

 2384 
 2385 -- | Structured error type for parser-level errors.
 2386 --
 2387 --   `HappyError` is generated when Happy calls its @%error@ function.
 2388 --   The other cases are generated by our own code below.
 2389 data ParseError
 2390   = HappyError [Token Pos] [String]
 2391   | InvalidPattern Pos Expr
 2392   | EmptyBlock Pos
 2393   | InvalidBlock Pos
 2394 
 2395 -- | Render a parse error.
 2396 --
 2397 -- For `HappyError` (the other messages are straightforward):
 2398 --
 2399 -- Happy's error reporting model is that it gives you the remaining
 2400 -- tokens, and the error message is effectively just "syntax error".
 2401 --
 2402 -- When the "%error.expected" flag is set, an extra argument is passed
 2403 -- to the parse error function. It's a list of strings that represent,
 2404 -- in some unspecified way, the legal next tokens at the point where
 2405 -- the error happened.
 2406 --
 2407 -- Why it doesn't just produce a list of tokens, IDK. I guess it has
 2408 -- no way to manufacture a value for a token that has a value and they
 2409 -- didn't want to come up with a mechanism to get one?
 2410 --
 2411 -- There is also apparently no way to discover
 2412 --    - the last token consumed
 2413 --    - the nonterminal(s) we're currently in the middle of
 2414 --    - which parser entry point we started from
 2415 --
 2416 -- all of which are things it's quite reasonable to kind of want to
 2417 -- know to produce a decent message. In place of the latter we have
 2418 -- the loader pass us the string to use as the token name for EOF.
 2419 --
 2420 -- So what we do is:
 2421 --    - If there is exactly one legal possible next input, we report
 2422 --      it as missing.
 2423 --    - Otherwise we say "Unexpected foo" and print the list of
 2424 --      possible inputs.
 2425 --
 2426 -- We trust that the strings Happy sends us will be meaningful to
 2427 -- the user. Good luck with that.
 2428 --
 2429 -- Note: we return the position and the document separately so they
 2430 -- can be passed to the error infrastructure separately.
 2431 --
 2432 prettyParseError :: Text -> ParseError -> (Maybe Pos, PPS.Doc)
 2433 prettyParseError eofName pe = case pe of
 2434     HappyError nextToks possibles ->
 2435         let (optpos, tstr) = case nextToks of
 2436               [] -> (Nothing, eofName)
 2437               t : _ts -> (Just (tokPos t), tokStr t)
 2438             tstr' = PPS.squotesMatching $ PP.pretty tstr
 2439             doc = case possibles of
 2440               [] -> "Syntax error: unexpected" PP.<+> tstr'
 2441               [p] -> "Syntax error: missing" PP.<+> PP.pretty p
 2442               ps ->
 2443                   let ps' =
 2444                         "Some legal inputs at this point:" : map PP.pretty ps
 2445                   in
 2446                   PP.vsep [
 2447                       "Syntax error: unexpected" PP.<+> tstr',
 2448                       PP.nest 3 $ PP.group $ PP.fillSep $ ps'
 2449                   ]
 2450         in
 2451         (optpos, doc)
 2452     InvalidPattern pos e ->
 2453         (Just pos, "Parse error: invalid pattern" PP.<+> PPS.prettyPrec 0 e)
 2454     EmptyBlock pos ->
 2455         (Just pos, "do block must include at least one expression")
 2456     InvalidBlock pos ->
 2457         (Just pos, "do block must end with expression")
 2458 
 2459 parseError :: [Token Pos] -> [String] -> Either ParseError b
 2460 parseError toks possibles =
 2461   Left (HappyError toks possibles)
 2462 
 2463 -- | Cons up an import.
 2464 buildImport ::
 2465     Bool ->
 2466     (Either FilePath P.ModName, Pos) ->
 2467     (Maybe P.ModName, Pos) ->
 2468     (Maybe P.ImportSpec, Pos) ->
 2469     Import
 2470 buildImport issub (modName, namePos) (mbAsName, asPos) (mbSpec, specPos) =
 2471   Import {
 2472     iIsSubmodule = issub,
 2473     iModule = modName,
 2474     iAs = mbAsName,
 2475     iSpec = mbSpec,
 2476     iPos = maxSpan [namePos, asPos, specPos]
 2477   }
 2478 
 2479 -- | As seen by the parser, a "function name" is an arbitrary pattern.
 2480 --   This is because we use the same syntax for function and value bindings:
 2481 --   in "let (a, b) = e" the "(a, b)" can and should be an arbitrary pattern.
 2482 --   For functions it doesn't make sense for it to be anything but a plain
 2483 --   name, as in "let f () = e". You can write "let (a, b) () = e" and the
 2484 --   parser will accept it, but it won't typecheck.
 2485 --
 2486 --   This function extracts the actual name, if any, for annotating
 2487 --   the lambda expressions we turn further arguments into. It will
 2488 --   return Nothing if the name is something other than an actual
 2489 --   name, which is fine for value bindings since the result won't be
 2490 --   used and also fine for nonsense like "let (a, b) () = e" that'll
 2491 --   be rejected by the typechecker. The annotations in question are
 2492 --   used only at eval time.
 2493 --
 2494 --   Runs in the Maybe monad for convenience.
 2495 fixFunctionName :: Maybe Pattern -> Maybe Text
 2496 fixFunctionName mname = do
 2497   name <- mname
 2498   case name of
 2499       PWild {} -> Nothing
 2500       PVar _allpos _namepos name _ty -> Just name
 2501       PTuple {} -> Nothing
 2502 
 2503 buildFunction :: Maybe Pattern -> [Pattern] -> Expr -> Expr
 2504 buildFunction mname args e =
 2505   let mname' = fixFunctionName mname
 2506       once :: Pattern -> Expr -> Expr
 2507       once pat e = Lambda (maxSpan' pat e) mname' pat e
 2508   in
 2509   foldr once e args
 2510 
 2511 buildApplication :: [Expr] -> Expr
 2512 buildApplication es =
 2513   foldl1 (\e body -> Application (maxSpan' e body) e body) es
 2514 
 2515 -- | Build a let-statement.
 2516 buildLet :: Pos -> Decl -> Stmt
 2517 buildLet pos d =
 2518   StmtLet pos ReadOnlyVar (NonRecursive d)
 2519 
 2520 -- | Build a rebindable let-statement.
 2521 buildLetRB :: Pos -> Decl -> Stmt
 2522 buildLetRB pos d =
 2523   StmtLet pos RebindableVar (NonRecursive d)
 2524 
 2525 -- | Build a rec-statement.
 2526 buildRec :: Pos -> [Decl] -> Stmt
 2527 buildRec pos ds =
 2528   StmtLet pos ReadOnlyVar (Recursive ds)
 2529 
 2530 -- | Build a variable-pattern. Discard the variable if it's _.
 2531 --
 2532 --   Note: it is probably more appropriate to discard all variables
 2533 --   that _begin_ with an underscore; however, the traditional usage
 2534 --   in ML, Haskell, and also Rust is to treat variables beginning
 2535 --   with underscore as placeholder variables that can still be used
 2536 --   behind your back. That's wrong; however, SAWScript is not the
 2537 --   place to fight this battle...
 2538 --
 2539 buildPVar :: Pos -> Pos -> Text -> Maybe Type -> Pattern
 2540 buildPVar allpos xpos x mty =
 2541   case x of
 2542     "_" -> PWild allpos mty
 2543     _ -> PVar allpos xpos x mty
 2544 
 2545 -- | Pop off the last statement in a do-block, which is required to
 2546 --   be a plain expression, and unpack it to an expression.
 2547 buildBlock :: Pos -> [Stmt] -> Either ParseError Expr
 2548 buildBlock pos stmts = case reverse stmts of
 2549   StmtBind _spos (PWild _patpos _noty) e : revstmts' ->
 2550     Right $ Block pos (reverse revstmts', e)
 2551   [] ->
 2552     Left $ EmptyBlock pos
 2553   _ ->
 2554     Left $ InvalidBlock pos
 2555 
 2556 toPattern :: Expr -> Either ParseError Pattern
 2557 toPattern expr =
 2558   case expr of
 2559     Tuple pos es ->
 2560         PTuple pos `fmap` mapM toPattern es
 2561     TSig pos (Var xpos x) t ->
 2562         return (buildPVar pos xpos x (Just t))
 2563     Var pos x ->
 2564         return (buildPVar pos pos x Nothing)
 2565     _ ->
 2566         Left (InvalidPattern (getPos expr) expr)

 2577 -- Do not remove this comment. Required to fix CPP parsing when using GCC and a clang-compiled alex.
 2578 #define LT(n,m) ((Happy_GHC_Exts.tagToEnum# (n Happy_GHC_Exts.<# m)) :: Happy_Prelude.Bool)
 2579 #define GTE(n,m) ((Happy_GHC_Exts.tagToEnum# (n Happy_GHC_Exts.>=# m)) :: Happy_Prelude.Bool)
 2580 #define EQ(n,m) ((Happy_GHC_Exts.tagToEnum# (n Happy_GHC_Exts.==# m)) :: Happy_Prelude.Bool)
 2581 #define PLUS(n,m) (n Happy_GHC_Exts.+# m)
 2582 #define MINUS(n,m) (n Happy_GHC_Exts.-# m)
 2583 #define TIMES(n,m) (n Happy_GHC_Exts.*# m)
 2584 #define NEGATE(n) (Happy_GHC_Exts.negateInt# (n))

 2587 data Happy_IntList = HappyCons Happy_Int Happy_IntList

 2589 #define INVALID_TOK -1#
 2590 #define ERROR_TOK 0#
 2591 #define CATCH_TOK 1#

 2593 #if defined(HAPPY_COERCE)
 2594 #  define GET_ERROR_TOKEN(x)  (case Happy_GHC_Exts.unsafeCoerce# x of { (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# i) -> i })
 2595 #  define MK_ERROR_TOKEN(i)   (Happy_GHC_Exts.unsafeCoerce# (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# i))
 2596 #  define MK_TOKEN(x)         (happyInTok (x))
 2597 #else
 2598 #  define GET_ERROR_TOKEN(x)  (case x of { HappyErrorToken (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# i) -> i })
 2599 #  define MK_ERROR_TOKEN(i)   (HappyErrorToken (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# i))
 2600 #  define MK_TOKEN(x)         (HappyTerminal (x))
 2601 #endif

 2603 #if defined(HAPPY_DEBUG)
 2604 #  define DEBUG_TRACE(s)    (happyTrace (s)) Happy_Prelude.$
 2605 happyTrace string expr = Happy_System_IO_Unsafe.unsafePerformIO Happy_Prelude.$ do
 2606     Happy_System_IO.hPutStr Happy_System_IO.stderr string
 2607     Happy_Prelude.return expr
 2608 #else
 2609 #  define DEBUG_TRACE(s)    {- nothing -}
 2610 #endif
 2611 
 2612 infixr 9 `HappyStk`
 2613 data HappyStk a = HappyStk a (HappyStk a)
 2614 
 2615 -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
 2616 -- starting the parse
 2617 
 2618 happyDoParse start_state = happyNewToken start_state notHappyAtAll notHappyAtAll
 2619 
 2620 -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
 2621 -- Accepting the parse
 2622 
 2623 -- If the current token is ERROR_TOK, it means we've just accepted a partial
 2624 -- parse (a %partial parser).  We must ignore the saved token on the top of
 2625 -- the stack in this case.
 2626 happyAccept ERROR_TOK tk st sts (_ `HappyStk` ans `HappyStk` _) =
 2627         happyReturn1 ans
 2628 happyAccept j tk st sts (HappyStk ans _) =
 2629         (happyTcHack j (happyTcHack st)) (happyReturn1 ans)
 2630 
 2631 -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
 2632 -- Arrays only: do the next action
 2633 
 2634 happyDoAction i tk st =
 2635   DEBUG_TRACE("state: " Happy_Prelude.++ Happy_Prelude.show (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# st) Happy_Prelude.++
 2636               ",\ttoken: " Happy_Prelude.++ Happy_Prelude.show (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# i) Happy_Prelude.++
 2637               ",\taction: ")
 2638   case happyDecodeAction (happyNextAction i st) of
 2639     HappyFail             -> DEBUG_TRACE("failing.\n")
 2640                              happyFail i tk st
 2641     HappyAccept           -> DEBUG_TRACE("accept.\n")
 2642                              happyAccept i tk st
 2643     HappyReduce rule      -> DEBUG_TRACE("reduce (rule " Happy_Prelude.++ Happy_Prelude.show (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# rule) Happy_Prelude.++ ")")
 2644                              (happyReduceArr Happy_Data_Array.! (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# rule)) i tk st
 2645     HappyShift  new_state -> DEBUG_TRACE("shift, enter state " Happy_Prelude.++ Happy_Prelude.show (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# new_state) Happy_Prelude.++ "\n")
 2646                              happyShift new_state i tk st
 2647 
 2648 {-# INLINE happyNextAction #-}
 2649 happyNextAction i st = case happyIndexActionTable i st of
 2650   Happy_Prelude.Just (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# act) -> act
 2651   Happy_Prelude.Nothing                      -> happyIndexOffAddr happyDefActions st
 2652 
 2653 {-# INLINE happyIndexActionTable #-}
 2654 happyIndexActionTable i st
 2655   | GTE(i, 0#), GTE(off, 0#), EQ(happyIndexOffAddr happyCheck off, i)
 2656   -- i >= 0:   Guard against INVALID_TOK (do the default action, which ultimately errors)
 2657   -- off >= 0: Otherwise it's a default action
 2658   -- equality check: Ensure that the entry in the compressed array is owned by st
 2659   = Happy_Prelude.Just (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# (happyIndexOffAddr happyTable off))
 2660   | Happy_Prelude.otherwise
 2661   = Happy_Prelude.Nothing
 2662   where
 2663     off = PLUS(happyIndexOffAddr happyActOffsets st, i)             
 2664 
 2665 data HappyAction
 2666   = HappyFail
 2667   | HappyAccept
 2668   | HappyReduce Happy_Int -- rule number
 2669   | HappyShift Happy_Int  -- new state
 2670   deriving Happy_Prelude.Show
 2671 
 2672 {-# INLINE happyDecodeAction #-}
 2673 happyDecodeAction :: Happy_Int -> HappyAction
 2674 happyDecodeAction  0#                        = HappyFail
 2675 happyDecodeAction -1#                        = HappyAccept
 2676 happyDecodeAction action | LT(action, 0#)    = HappyReduce NEGATE(PLUS(action, 1#))
 2677                          | Happy_Prelude.otherwise = HappyShift MINUS(action, 1#)            
 2678 
 2679 {-# INLINE happyIndexGotoTable #-}
 2680 happyIndexGotoTable nt st = happyIndexOffAddr happyTable off
 2681   where
 2682     off = PLUS(happyIndexOffAddr happyGotoOffsets st, nt)             
 2683 
 2684 {-# INLINE happyIndexOffAddr #-}
 2685 happyIndexOffAddr :: HappyAddr -> Happy_Int -> Happy_Int
 2686 happyIndexOffAddr (HappyA# arr) off =
 2687 #if __GLASGOW_HASKELL__ >= 901
 2688   Happy_GHC_Exts.int32ToInt# -- qualified import because it doesn't exist on older GHC's
 2689 #endif
 2690 #ifdef WORDS_BIGENDIAN
 2691   -- The CI of `alex` tests this code path
 2692   (Happy_GHC_Exts.word32ToInt32# (Happy_GHC_Exts.wordToWord32# (Happy_GHC_Exts.byteSwap32# (Happy_GHC_Exts.word32ToWord# (Happy_GHC_Exts.int32ToWord32#
 2693 #endif
 2694   (Happy_GHC_Exts.indexInt32OffAddr# arr off)
 2695 #ifdef WORDS_BIGENDIAN
 2696   )))))
 2697 #endif
 2698 
 2699 happyIndexRuleArr :: Happy_Int -> (# Happy_Int, Happy_Int #)
 2700 happyIndexRuleArr r = (# nt, len #)
 2701   where
 2702     !(Happy_GHC_Exts.I# n_starts) = happy_n_starts
 2703     offs = TIMES(MINUS(r,n_starts),2#)
 2704     nt = happyIndexOffAddr happyRuleArr offs
 2705     len = happyIndexOffAddr happyRuleArr PLUS(offs,1#)             
 2706 
 2707 data HappyAddr = HappyA# Happy_GHC_Exts.Addr#
 2708 
 2709 -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
 2710 -- Shifting a token
 2711 
 2712 happyShift new_state ERROR_TOK tk st sts stk@(x `HappyStk` _) =
 2713      -- See "Error Fixup" below
 2714      let i = GET_ERROR_TOKEN(x) in
 2715      DEBUG_TRACE("shifting the error token")
 2716      happyDoAction i tk new_state (HappyCons st sts) stk
 2717 
 2718 happyShift new_state i tk st sts stk =
 2719      happyNewToken new_state (HappyCons st sts) (MK_TOKEN(tk) `HappyStk` stk)    
 2720 
 2721 -- happyReduce is specialised for the common cases.
 2722 
 2723 happySpecReduce_0 nt fn j tk st sts stk
 2724      = happySeq fn (happyGoto nt j tk st (HappyCons st sts) (fn `HappyStk` stk))
 2725 
 2726 happySpecReduce_1 nt fn j tk old_st sts@(HappyCons st _) (v1 `HappyStk` stk')
 2727      = let r = fn v1 in
 2728        happyTcHack old_st (happySeq r (happyGoto nt j tk st sts (r `HappyStk` stk')))
 2729 
 2730 happySpecReduce_2 nt fn j tk old_st
 2731   (HappyCons _ sts@(HappyCons st _))
 2732   (v1 `HappyStk` v2 `HappyStk` stk')
 2733      = let r = fn v1 v2 in
 2734        happyTcHack old_st (happySeq r (happyGoto nt j tk st sts (r `HappyStk` stk')))
 2735 
 2736 happySpecReduce_3 nt fn j tk old_st
 2737   (HappyCons _ (HappyCons _ sts@(HappyCons st _)))
 2738   (v1 `HappyStk` v2 `HappyStk` v3 `HappyStk` stk')
 2739      = let r = fn v1 v2 v3 in
 2740        happyTcHack old_st (happySeq r (happyGoto nt j tk st sts (r `HappyStk` stk')))
 2741 
 2742 happyReduce k nt fn j tk st sts stk
 2743      = case happyDrop MINUS(k,(1# :: Happy_Int)) sts of
 2744          sts1@(HappyCons st1 _) ->
 2745                 let r = fn stk in -- it doesn't hurt to always seq here...
 2746                 st `happyTcHack` happyDoSeq r (happyGoto nt j tk st1 sts1 r)
 2747 
 2748 happyMonadReduce k nt fn j tk st sts stk =
 2749       case happyDrop k (HappyCons st sts) of
 2750         sts1@(HappyCons st1 _) ->
 2751           let drop_stk = happyDropStk k stk in
 2752           j `happyTcHack` happyThen1 (fn stk tk)
 2753                                      (\r -> happyGoto nt j tk st1 sts1 (r `HappyStk` drop_stk))
 2754 
 2755 happyMonad2Reduce k nt fn j tk st sts stk =
 2756       case happyDrop k (HappyCons st sts) of
 2757         sts1@(HappyCons st1 _) ->
 2758           let drop_stk = happyDropStk k stk
 2759               off = happyIndexOffAddr happyGotoOffsets st1
 2760               off_i = PLUS(off, nt)
 2761               new_state = happyIndexOffAddr happyTable off_i
 2762           in
 2763             j `happyTcHack` happyThen1 (fn stk tk)
 2764                                        (\r -> happyNewToken new_state sts1 (r `HappyStk` drop_stk))
 2765 
 2766 happyDrop 0# l               = l
 2767 happyDrop n  (HappyCons _ t) = happyDrop MINUS(n,(1# :: Happy_Int)) t            
 2768 
 2769 happyDropStk 0# l                 = l
 2770 happyDropStk n  (x `HappyStk` xs) = happyDropStk MINUS(n,(1#::Happy_Int)) xs            
 2771 
 2772 -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
 2773 -- Moving to a new state after a reduction
 2774 
 2775 happyGoto nt j tk st =
 2776    DEBUG_TRACE(", goto state " Happy_Prelude.++ Happy_Prelude.show (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# new_state) Happy_Prelude.++ "\n")
 2777    happyDoAction j tk new_state
 2778   where new_state = happyIndexGotoTable nt st
 2779 
 2780 {- Note [Error recovery]
 2781 ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
 2782 When there is no applicable action for the current lookahead token `tk`,
 2783 happy enters error recovery mode. Depending on whether the grammar file
 2784 declares the two action form `%error { abort } { report }` for
 2785     Resumptive Error Handling,
 2786 it works in one (not resumptive) or two phases (resumptive):
 2787 
 2788  1. Fixup mode:
 2789     Try to see if there is an action for the error token ERROR_TOK. If there
 2790     is, do *not* emit an error and pretend instead that an `error` token was
 2791     inserted.
 2792     When there is no ERROR_TOK action, report an error.
 2793 
 2794     In non-resumptive error handling, calling the single error handler
 2795     (e.g. `happyError`) will throw an exception and abort the parser.
 2796     However, in resumptive error handling we enter *error resumption mode*.
 2797 
 2798  2. Error resumption mode:
 2799     After reporting the error (with `report`), happy will attempt to find
 2800     a good state stack to resume parsing in.
 2801     For each candidate stack, it discards input until one of the candidates
 2802     resumes (i.e. shifts the current input).
 2803     If no candidate resumes before the end of input, resumption failed and
 2804     calls the `abort` function, to much the same effect as in non-resumptive
 2805     error handling.
 2806 
 2807     Candidate stacks are declared by the grammar author using the special
 2808     `catch` terminal and called "catch frames".
 2809     This mechanism is described in detail in Note [happyResume].
 2810 
 2811 The `catch` resumption mechanism (2) is what usually is associated with
 2812 `error` in `bison` or `menhir`. Since `error` is used for the Fixup mechanism
 2813 (1) above, we call the corresponding token `catch`.
 2814 Furthermore, in constrast to `bison`, our implementation of `catch`
 2815 non-deterministically considers multiple catch frames on the stack for
 2816 resumption (See Note [Multiple catch frames]).
 2817 
 2818 Note [happyResume]
 2819 ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
 2820 `happyResume` implements the resumption mechanism from Note [Error recovery].
 2821 It is best understood by example. Consider
 2822 
 2823 Exp :: { String }
 2824 Exp : '1'                { "1" }
 2825     | catch              { "catch" }
 2826     | Exp '+' Exp %shift { $1 Happy_Prelude.++ " + " Happy_Prelude.++ $3 } -- %shift: associate 1 + 1 + 1 to the right
 2827     | '(' Exp ')'        { "(" Happy_Prelude.++ $2 Happy_Prelude.++ ")" }
 2828 
 2829 The idea of the use of `catch` here is that upon encountering a parse error
 2830 during expression parsing, we can gracefully degrade using the `catch` rule,
 2831 still producing a partial syntax tree and keep on parsing to find further
 2832 syntax errors.
 2833 
 2834 Let's trace the parser state for input 11+1, which will error out after shifting 1.
 2835 After shifting, we have the following item stack (growing downwards and omitting
 2836 transitive closure items):
 2837 
 2838   State 0: %start_parseExp -> . Exp
 2839   State 5: Exp -> '1' .
 2840 
 2841 (Stack as a list of state numbers: [5,0].)
 2842 As Note [Error recovery] describes, we will first try Fixup mode.
 2843 That fails because no production can shift the `error` token.
 2844 Next we try Error resumption mode. This works as follows:
 2845 
 2846   1. Pop off the item stack until we find an item that can shift the `catch`
 2847      token. (Implemented in `pop_items`.)
 2848        * State 5 cannot shift catch. Pop.
 2849        * State 0 can shift catch, which would transition into
 2850           State 4: Exp -> catch .
 2851      So record the *stack* `[4,0]` after doing the shift transition.
 2852      We call this a *catch frame*, where the top is a *catch state*,
 2853      corresponding to an item in which we just shifted a `catch` token.
 2854      There can be multiple such catch stacks, see Note [Multiple catch frames].
 2855 
 2856   2. Discard tokens from the input until the lookahead can be shifted in one
 2857      of the catch stacks. (Implemented in `discard_input_until_exp` and
 2858      `some_catch_state_shifts`.)
 2859        * We cannot shift the current lookahead '1' in state 4, so we discard
 2860        * We *can* shift the next lookahead '+' in state 4, but only after
 2861          reducing, which pops State 4 and goes to State 3:
 2862            State 3: %start_parseExp -> Exp .
 2863                     Exp -> Exp . '+' Exp
 2864          Here we can shift '+'.
 2865      As you can see, to implement this machinery we need to simulate
 2866      the operation of the LALR automaton, especially reduction
 2867      (`happySimulateReduce`).
 2868 
 2869 Note [Multiple catch frames]
 2870 ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
 2871 For fewer spurious error messages, it can be beneficial to trace multiple catch
 2872 items. Consider
 2873 
 2874 Exp : '1'
 2875     | catch
 2876     | Exp '+' Exp %shift
 2877     | '(' Exp ')'
 2878 
 2879 Let's trace the parser state for input (;+1, which will error out after shifting (.
 2880 After shifting, we have the following item stack (growing downwards):
 2881 
 2882   State 0: %start_parseExp -> . Exp
 2883   State 6: Exp -> '(' . Exp ')'
 2884 
 2885 Upon error, we want to find items in the stack which can shift a catch token.
 2886 Note that both State 0 and State 6 can shift a catch token, transitioning into
 2887   State 4: Exp -> catch .
 2888 Hence we record the catch frames `[4,6,0]` and `[4,0]` for possible resumption.
 2889 
 2890 Which catch frame do we pick for resumption?
 2891 Note that resuming catch frame `[4,0]` will parse as "catch+1", whereas
 2892 resuming the innermost frame `[4,6,0]` corresponds to parsing "(catch+1".
 2893 The latter would keep discarding input until the closing ')' is found.
 2894 So we will discard + and 1, leading to a spurious syntax error at the end of
 2895 input, aborting the parse and never producing a partial syntax tree. Bad!
 2896 
 2897 It is far preferable to resume with catch frame `[4,0]`, where we can resume
 2898 successfully on input +, so that is what we do.
 2899 
 2900 In general, we pick the catch frame for resumption that discards the least
 2901 amount of input for a successful shift, preferring the topmost such catch frame.
 2902 -}
 2903 
 2904 -- happyFail :: Happy_Int -> Token -> Happy_Int -> _
 2905 -- This function triggers Note [Error recovery].
 2906 -- If the current token is ERROR_TOK, phase (1) has failed and we might try
 2907 -- phase (2).
 2908 happyFail ERROR_TOK = happyFixupFailed
 2909 happyFail i         = happyTryFixup i
 2910 
 2911 -- Enter Error Fixup (see Note [Error recovery]):
 2912 -- generate an error token, save the old token and carry on.
 2913 -- When a `happyShift` accepts the error token, we will pop off the error token
 2914 -- to resume parsing with the current lookahead `i`.
 2915 happyTryFixup i tk action sts stk =
 2916   DEBUG_TRACE("entering `error` fixup.\n")
 2917   happyDoAction ERROR_TOK tk action sts (MK_ERROR_TOKEN(i) `HappyStk` stk)                          
 2918   -- NB: `happyShift` will simply pop the error token and carry on with
 2919   --     `tk`. Hence we don't change `tk` in the call here
 2920 
 2921 -- See Note [Error recovery], phase (2).
 2922 -- Enter resumption mode after reporting the error by calling `happyResume`.
 2923 happyFixupFailed tk st sts (x `HappyStk` stk) =
 2924   let i = GET_ERROR_TOKEN(x) in
 2925   DEBUG_TRACE("`error` fixup failed.\n")
 2926   let resume   = happyResume i tk st sts stk
 2927       expected = happyExpectedTokens st sts in
 2928   happyReport i tk expected resume
 2929 
 2930 -- happyResume :: Happy_Int -> Token -> Happy_Int -> _
 2931 -- See Note [happyResume]
 2932 happyResume i tk st sts stk = pop_items [] st sts stk
 2933   where
 2934     !(Happy_GHC_Exts.I# n_starts) = happy_n_starts   -- this is to test whether we have a start token
 2935     !(Happy_GHC_Exts.I# eof_i) = happy_n_terms Happy_Prelude.- 1   -- this is the token number of the EOF token
 2936     happy_list_to_list :: Happy_IntList -> [Happy_Prelude.Int]
 2937     happy_list_to_list (HappyCons st sts)
 2938       | LT(st, n_starts)
 2939       = [(Happy_GHC_Exts.I# st)]
 2940       | Happy_Prelude.otherwise
 2941       = (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# st) : happy_list_to_list sts
 2942 
 2943     -- See (1) of Note [happyResume]
 2944     pop_items catch_frames st sts stk
 2945       | LT(st, n_starts)
 2946       = DEBUG_TRACE("reached start state " Happy_Prelude.++ Happy_Prelude.show (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# st) Happy_Prelude.++ ", ")
 2947         if Happy_Prelude.null catch_frames_new
 2948           then DEBUG_TRACE("no resumption.\n")
 2949                happyAbort
 2950           else DEBUG_TRACE("now discard input, trying to anchor in states " Happy_Prelude.++ Happy_Prelude.show (Happy_Prelude.map (happy_list_to_list . Happy_Prelude.fst) (Happy_Prelude.reverse catch_frames_new)) Happy_Prelude.++ ".\n")
 2951                discard_input_until_exp i tk (Happy_Prelude.reverse catch_frames_new)
 2952       | (HappyCons st1 sts1) <- sts, _ `HappyStk` stk1 <- stk
 2953       = pop_items catch_frames_new st1 sts1 stk1
 2954       where
 2955         !catch_frames_new
 2956           | HappyShift new_state <- happyDecodeAction (happyNextAction CATCH_TOK st)
 2957           , DEBUG_TRACE("can shift catch token in state " Happy_Prelude.++ Happy_Prelude.show (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# st) Happy_Prelude.++ ", into state " Happy_Prelude.++ Happy_Prelude.show (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# new_state) Happy_Prelude.++ "\n")
 2958             Happy_Prelude.null (Happy_Prelude.filter (\(HappyCons _ (HappyCons h _),_) -> EQ(st,h)) catch_frames)
 2959           = (HappyCons new_state (HappyCons st sts), MK_ERROR_TOKEN(i) `HappyStk` stk):catch_frames -- MK_ERROR_TOKEN(i) is just some dummy that should not be accessed by user code
 2960           | Happy_Prelude.otherwise
 2961           = DEBUG_TRACE("already shifted or can't shift catch in " Happy_Prelude.++ Happy_Prelude.show (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# st) Happy_Prelude.++ "\n")
 2962             catch_frames
 2963 
 2964     -- See (2) of Note [happyResume]
 2965     discard_input_until_exp i tk catch_frames
 2966       | Happy_Prelude.Just (HappyCons st (HappyCons catch_st sts), catch_frame) <- some_catch_state_shifts i catch_frames
 2967       = DEBUG_TRACE("found expected token in state " Happy_Prelude.++ Happy_Prelude.show (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# st) Happy_Prelude.++ " after shifting from " Happy_Prelude.++ Happy_Prelude.show (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# catch_st) Happy_Prelude.++ ": " Happy_Prelude.++ Happy_Prelude.show (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# i) Happy_Prelude.++ "\n")
 2968         happyDoAction i tk st (HappyCons catch_st sts) catch_frame
 2969       | EQ(i,eof_i) -- is i EOF?
 2970       = DEBUG_TRACE("reached EOF, cannot resume. abort parse :(\n")
 2971         happyAbort
 2972       | Happy_Prelude.otherwise
 2973       = DEBUG_TRACE("discard token " Happy_Prelude.++ Happy_Prelude.show (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# i) Happy_Prelude.++ "\n")
 2974         happyLex (\eof_tk -> discard_input_until_exp eof_i eof_tk catch_frames) -- eof
 2975                  (\i tk   -> discard_input_until_exp i tk catch_frames)         -- not eof
 2976 
 2977     some_catch_state_shifts _ [] = DEBUG_TRACE("no catch state could shift.\n") Happy_Prelude.Nothing
 2978     some_catch_state_shifts i catch_frames@(((HappyCons st sts),_):_) = try_head i st sts catch_frames
 2979       where
 2980         try_head i st sts catch_frames = -- PRECONDITION: head catch_frames = (HappyCons st sts)
 2981           DEBUG_TRACE("trying token " Happy_Prelude.++ Happy_Prelude.show (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# i) Happy_Prelude.++ " in state " Happy_Prelude.++ Happy_Prelude.show (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# st) Happy_Prelude.++ ": ")
 2982           case happyDecodeAction (happyNextAction i st) of
 2983             HappyFail     -> DEBUG_TRACE("fail.\n")   some_catch_state_shifts i (Happy_Prelude.tail catch_frames)
 2984             HappyAccept   -> DEBUG_TRACE("accept.\n") Happy_Prelude.Just (Happy_Prelude.head catch_frames)
 2985             HappyShift _  -> DEBUG_TRACE("shift.\n")  Happy_Prelude.Just (Happy_Prelude.head catch_frames)
 2986             HappyReduce r -> case happySimulateReduce r st sts of
 2987               (HappyCons st1 sts1) -> try_head i st1 sts1 catch_frames
 2988 
 2989 happySimulateReduce r st sts =
 2990   DEBUG_TRACE("simulate reduction of rule " Happy_Prelude.++ Happy_Prelude.show (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# r) Happy_Prelude.++ ", ")
 2991   let (# nt, len #) = happyIndexRuleArr r in
 2992   DEBUG_TRACE("nt " Happy_Prelude.++ Happy_Prelude.show (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# nt) Happy_Prelude.++ ", len: " Happy_Prelude.++ Happy_Prelude.show (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# len) Happy_Prelude.++ ", new_st ")
 2993   let !(sts1@(HappyCons st1 _)) = happyDrop len (HappyCons st sts)
 2994       new_st = happyIndexGotoTable nt st1 in
 2995   DEBUG_TRACE(Happy_Prelude.show (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# new_st) Happy_Prelude.++ ".\n")
 2996   (HappyCons new_st sts1)
 2997 
 2998 happyTokenToString :: Happy_Prelude.Int -> Happy_Prelude.String
 2999 happyTokenToString i = happyTokenStrings Happy_Prelude.!! (i Happy_Prelude.- 2) -- 2: errorTok, catchTok
 3000 
 3001 happyExpectedTokens :: Happy_Int -> Happy_IntList -> [Happy_Prelude.String]
 3002 -- Upon a parse error, we want to suggest tokens that are expected in that
 3003 -- situation. This function computes such tokens.
 3004 -- It works by examining the top of the state stack.
 3005 -- For every token number that does a shift transition, record that token number.
 3006 -- For every token number that does a reduce transition, simulate that reduction
 3007 -- on the state state stack and repeat.
 3008 -- The recorded token numbers are then formatted with 'happyTokenToString' and
 3009 -- returned.
 3010 happyExpectedTokens st sts =
 3011   DEBUG_TRACE("constructing expected tokens.\n")
 3012   Happy_Prelude.map happyTokenToString (search_shifts st sts [])
 3013   where
 3014     search_shifts st sts shifts = Happy_Prelude.foldr (add_action st sts) shifts (distinct_actions st)
 3015     add_action st sts (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# i, Happy_GHC_Exts.I# act) shifts =
 3016       DEBUG_TRACE("found action in state " Happy_Prelude.++ Happy_Prelude.show (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# st) Happy_Prelude.++ ", input " Happy_Prelude.++ Happy_Prelude.show (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# i) Happy_Prelude.++ ", " Happy_Prelude.++ Happy_Prelude.show (happyDecodeAction act) Happy_Prelude.++ "\n")
 3017       case happyDecodeAction act of
 3018         HappyFail     -> shifts
 3019         HappyAccept   -> shifts -- This would always be %eof or error... Not helpful
 3020         HappyShift _  -> Happy_Prelude.insert (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# i) shifts
 3021         HappyReduce r -> case happySimulateReduce r st sts of
 3022           (HappyCons st1 sts1) -> search_shifts st1 sts1 shifts
 3023     distinct_actions st
 3024       -- The (token number, action) pairs of all actions in the given state
 3025       = ((-1), (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# (happyIndexOffAddr happyDefActions st)))
 3026       : [ (i, act) | i <- [begin_i..happy_n_terms], act <- get_act row_off i ]
 3027       where
 3028         row_off = happyIndexOffAddr happyActOffsets st
 3029         begin_i = 2 -- +2: errorTok,catchTok
 3030     get_act off (Happy_GHC_Exts.I# i) -- happyIndexActionTable with cached row offset
 3031       | let off_i = PLUS(off,i)
 3032       , GTE(off_i,0#)
 3033       , EQ(happyIndexOffAddr happyCheck off_i,i)
 3034       = [(Happy_GHC_Exts.I# (happyIndexOffAddr happyTable off_i))]
 3035       | Happy_Prelude.otherwise
 3036       = []
 3037 
 3038 -- Internal happy errors:
 3039 
 3040 notHappyAtAll :: a
 3041 notHappyAtAll = Happy_Prelude.error "Internal Happy parser panic. This is not supposed to happen! Please open a bug report at https://github.com/haskell/happy/issues.\n"
 3042 
 3043 -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
 3044 -- Hack to get the typechecker to accept our action functions
 3045 
 3046 happyTcHack :: Happy_Int -> a -> a
 3047 happyTcHack x y = y
 3048 {-# INLINE happyTcHack #-}
 3049 
 3050 -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
 3051 -- Seq-ing.  If the --strict flag is given, then Happy emits
 3052 --      happySeq = happyDoSeq
 3053 -- otherwise it emits
 3054 --      happySeq = happyDontSeq
 3055 
 3056 happyDoSeq, happyDontSeq :: a -> b -> b
 3057 happyDoSeq   a b = a `Happy_GHC_Exts.seq` b
 3058 happyDontSeq a b = b

 3061 -- Don't inline any functions from the template.  GHC has a nasty habit
 3062 -- of deciding to inline happyGoto everywhere, which increases the size of
 3063 -- the generated parser quite a bit.
 3064 
 3065 {-# NOINLINE happyDoAction #-}
 3066 {-# NOINLINE happyTable #-}
 3067 {-# NOINLINE happyCheck #-}
 3068 {-# NOINLINE happyActOffsets #-}
 3069 {-# NOINLINE happyGotoOffsets #-}
 3070 {-# NOINLINE happyDefActions #-}
 3071 
 3072 {-# NOINLINE happyShift #-}
 3073 {-# NOINLINE happySpecReduce_0 #-}
 3074 {-# NOINLINE happySpecReduce_1 #-}
 3075 {-# NOINLINE happySpecReduce_2 #-}
 3076 {-# NOINLINE happySpecReduce_3 #-}
 3077 {-# NOINLINE happyReduce #-}
 3078 {-# NOINLINE happyMonadReduce #-}
 3079 {-# NOINLINE happyGoto #-}
 3080 {-# NOINLINE happyFail #-}
